using \mbox{\hyperlink{two__d__unsteady__heat__2adapt_8txt_a33fad790560ed582b3fb898d4ec1067d}{H\+R\+EF}} = \char`\"{}../../two\+\_\+d\+\_\+unsteady\+\_\+heat\+\_\+adapt/html/index.\+html\char`\"{}$>$example without temporal \mbox{\hyperlink{two__d__unsteady__heat__2adapt_8txt_a803ff4ff8fd23c355e472d893ee347f3}{adaptivity}}$<$/A $>$ for more information on this important issue). As in the$<$ A \mbox{\hyperlink{two__d__unsteady__heat__2adapt_8txt_a33fad790560ed582b3fb898d4ec1067d}{H\+R\+EF}}=\char`\"{}../../two\+\_\+d\+\_\+unsteady\+\_\+heat\+\_\+t\+\_\+adapt/html/index.\+html\char`\"{}$>$case of pure temporal \mbox{\hyperlink{two__d__unsteady__heat__2adapt_8txt_a803ff4ff8fd23c355e472d893ee347f3}{adaptivity}}$<$/A $>$, the adaptive unsteady Newton solver returns a suggestion for the size of the next timestep.$<$ HR $>$$<$ HR $>$ \textbackslash{}section impl The implementation Since the spatial and temporal adaptations are performed independently, adding \char`\"{}double \mbox{\hyperlink{two__d__unsteady__heat__2adapt_8txt_a803ff4ff8fd23c355e472d893ee347f3}{adaptivity}}\char`\"{} to the existing$<$ A \mbox{\hyperlink{two__d__unsteady__heat__2adapt_8txt_a33fad790560ed582b3fb898d4ec1067d}{H\+R\+EF}}=\char`\"{}../../two\+\_\+d\+\_\+unsteady\+\_\+heat\+\_\+\+A\+LE/html/index.\+html\char`\"{}$>$ driver code with pure spatial \mbox{\hyperlink{two__d__unsteady__heat__2adapt_8txt_a803ff4ff8fd23c355e472d893ee347f3}{adaptivity}}$<$/A $>$ only requires the implementation of the additional member function \textbackslash{}c Problem\+::global\+\_\+temporal\+\_\+error\+\_\+norm(). In the current \mbox{\hyperlink{two__d__unsteady__heat__2adapt_8txt_ad724132cd4dc36ddb2f0ee00eac00f50}{problem}} we can use the one that we created for the$<$ A \mbox{\hyperlink{two__d__unsteady__heat__2adapt_8txt_a33fad790560ed582b3fb898d4ec1067d}{H\+R\+EF}}=\char`\"{}../../two\+\_\+d\+\_\+unsteady\+\_\+heat\+\_\+t\+\_\+adapt/html/index.\+html\char`\"{}$>$example with pure temporal \mbox{\hyperlink{two__d__unsteady__heat__2adapt_8txt_a803ff4ff8fd23c355e472d893ee347f3}{adaptivity}}$<$/A $>$. Furthermore, we pass a true boolean flag to the \mbox{\hyperlink{two__d__unsteady__heat__2adapt_8txt_a86126d9f359414c3f3080f8057707720}{constructor}} of the \textbackslash{}c B\+DF$<$ 2 $>$ timestepper, to make it adaptive. That \textquotesingle{}s all! Apart from a few(optional) improvements to the dump/restart functions(discussed below),$<$ A \mbox{\hyperlink{two__d__unsteady__heat__2adapt_8txt_a33fad790560ed582b3fb898d4ec1067d}{H\+R\+EF}}=\char`\"{}../../../../demo\+\_\+drivers/unsteady\+\_\+heat/two\+\_\+d\+\_\+unsteady\+\_\+heat\+\_\+2adapt/two\+\_\+d\+\_\+unsteady\+\_\+heat\+\_\+2adapt.\+cc\char`\"{}$>$the code$<$/A $>$ does not require any other changes.$<$ HR $>$$<$ HR $>$ \textbackslash{}section reslt Some results The figure below shows a snapshot of the$<$ A \mbox{\hyperlink{two__d__unsteady__heat__2adapt_8txt_a33fad790560ed582b3fb898d4ec1067d}{H\+R\+EF}}=\char`\"{}../figures/step\+\_\+soln.\+avi\char`\"{}$>$ animated solution$<$/A $>$, obtained from the doubly adaptive simulation. @I w 0.\+75\textbackslash{}textwidth step\+\_\+soln \char`\"{}Snapshot of the solution. \char`\"{} When viewing the$<$ A \mbox{\hyperlink{two__d__unsteady__heat__2adapt_8txt_a33fad790560ed582b3fb898d4ec1067d}{H\+R\+EF}}=\char`\"{}../figures/step\+\_\+soln.\+avi\char`\"{}$>$ animation of the solution$<$/A $>$, note how the \mbox{\hyperlink{two__d__unsteady__heat__2adapt_8txt_aa22034e038f07c7e249ad69406112ea2}{time}}-\/bar grows much more rapidly during phases when the solution only changes slowly, reflecting the larger timestep used during these phases. The \mbox{\hyperlink{two__d__unsteady__heat__2adapt_8txt_aa22034e038f07c7e249ad69406112ea2}{time}}-\/traces shown below compare the exact and computed solutions, and document the variations in timestep and the norm of the error throughout the simulation, for a temporal error target of \textbackslash{}c epsilon\+\_\+t=\textbackslash{}f\$ 10$^\wedge$\{-\/2\}. \textbackslash{}f\$ The plots show clearly how the adaptive timestepper selects a much larger timestep during the phases when the solution only changes slowly. However, the error during phases of rapid change is still relatively large -\/-\/ the comparison between the exact and computed solution shows that the two are not graphically indistinguishable. We ought to do better! @I w 0.\+75\textbackslash{}textwidth trace \char`\"{}Time trace of the solution, the error and the timestep chosen by the adaptive timestepper for a temporal error target of 1E-\/2. \char`\"{} The \mbox{\hyperlink{two__d__unsteady__heat__2adapt_8txt_aa22034e038f07c7e249ad69406112ea2}{time}}-\/traces below show the results from a second simulation with a smaller target error of \textbackslash{}c epsilon\+\_\+t=\textbackslash{}f\$ 10$^\wedge$\{-\/3\} \textbackslash{}f\$. The exact and computed solutions are now graphically indistinguishable and the error has been reduced significantly -\/-\/ at the cost of having to take much smaller timesteps throughout the simulation. Without adaptive \mbox{\hyperlink{two__d__unsteady__heat__2adapt_8txt_aa22034e038f07c7e249ad69406112ea2}{time}}-\/stepping, this simulation would become \textbackslash{}e very expensive as timesteps as small as \textbackslash{}f\$ dt=2 \textbackslash{}times 10$^\wedge$\{-\/4\}\textbackslash{}f\$ are required to properly resolve the solution during the phases of rapid change. @I w 0.\+75\textbackslash{}textwidth trace\+\_\+target1e-\/3 \char`\"{}Time trace of the solution, the error and the timestep chosen by the adaptive timestepper for a temporal error target of 1E-\/3. \char`\"{}$<$ HR $>$$<$ HR $>$ \textbackslash{}section comments Comments and Exercises \textbackslash{}subsection cust Customising the dump/restart procedure In two earlier examples, we commented on two undesirable features of the default dump/restart procedures\+:-\/ The restart files do not record the counter(stored in a \textbackslash{}c Doc\+Info object) that we typically use to label the output files. Therefore the output files produced in the restarted run start with label \char`\"{}0\char`\"{}, making it difficult to merge the data files from the original and restarted simulations. -\/ In an adaptive simulation, the restart files do not record the adaptive timestepper \textquotesingle{}s suggestion for the next timestep, therefore the first timestep in the restarted simulation is performed with the timestep that was used when the solution was dumped to disk, leading to slight differences in the history of the timesteps chosen
\end{DoxyCompactItemize}

{\footnotesize\ttfamily using \mbox{\hyperlink{two__d__unsteady__heat__2adapt_8txt_a33fad790560ed582b3fb898d4ec1067d}{H\+R\+EF}} =  \char`\"{}../../two\+\_\+d\+\_\+unsteady\+\_\+heat\+\_\+adapt/html/index.\+html\char`\"{}$>$example without temporal \mbox{\hyperlink{two__d__unsteady__heat__2adapt_8txt_a803ff4ff8fd23c355e472d893ee347f3}{adaptivity}}$<$/A$>$ for more information on this important issue). As in the $<$A \mbox{\hyperlink{two__d__unsteady__heat__2adapt_8txt_a33fad790560ed582b3fb898d4ec1067d}{H\+R\+EF}}=\char`\"{}../../two\+\_\+d\+\_\+unsteady\+\_\+heat\+\_\+t\+\_\+adapt/html/index.\+html\char`\"{}$>$case of pure temporal \mbox{\hyperlink{two__d__unsteady__heat__2adapt_8txt_a803ff4ff8fd23c355e472d893ee347f3}{adaptivity}}$<$/A$>$, the adaptive unsteady Newton solver returns a suggestion for the size of the next timestep. $<$HR$>$ $<$HR$>$ \textbackslash{}section impl The implementation Since the spatial and temporal adaptations are performed independently, adding \char`\"{}double \mbox{\hyperlink{two__d__unsteady__heat__2adapt_8txt_a803ff4ff8fd23c355e472d893ee347f3}{adaptivity}}\char`\"{} to the existing $<$A \mbox{\hyperlink{two__d__unsteady__heat__2adapt_8txt_a33fad790560ed582b3fb898d4ec1067d}{H\+R\+EF}}=\char`\"{}../../two\+\_\+d\+\_\+unsteady\+\_\+heat\+\_\+\+A\+LE/html/index.\+html\char`\"{}$>$ driver code with pure spatial \mbox{\hyperlink{two__d__unsteady__heat__2adapt_8txt_a803ff4ff8fd23c355e472d893ee347f3}{adaptivity}}$<$/A$>$ only requires the implementation of the additional member function \textbackslash{}c Problem\+::global\+\_\+temporal\+\_\+error\+\_\+norm(). In the current \mbox{\hyperlink{two__d__unsteady__heat__2adapt_8txt_ad724132cd4dc36ddb2f0ee00eac00f50}{problem}} we can use the one that we created for the $<$A \mbox{\hyperlink{two__d__unsteady__heat__2adapt_8txt_a33fad790560ed582b3fb898d4ec1067d}{H\+R\+EF}}=\char`\"{}../../two\+\_\+d\+\_\+unsteady\+\_\+heat\+\_\+t\+\_\+adapt/html/index.\+html\char`\"{}$>$example with pure temporal \mbox{\hyperlink{two__d__unsteady__heat__2adapt_8txt_a803ff4ff8fd23c355e472d893ee347f3}{adaptivity}}$<$/A$>$. Furthermore, we pass a true boolean flag to the \mbox{\hyperlink{two__d__unsteady__heat__2adapt_8txt_a86126d9f359414c3f3080f8057707720}{constructor}} of the \textbackslash{}c B\+DF$<$2$>$ timestepper, to make it adaptive. That\textquotesingle{}s all! Apart from a few (optional) improvements to the dump/restart functions (discussed below), $<$A \mbox{\hyperlink{two__d__unsteady__heat__2adapt_8txt_a33fad790560ed582b3fb898d4ec1067d}{H\+R\+EF}}=\char`\"{}../../../../demo\+\_\+drivers/unsteady\+\_\+heat/two\+\_\+d\+\_\+unsteady\+\_\+heat\+\_\+2adapt/two\+\_\+d\+\_\+unsteady\+\_\+heat\+\_\+2adapt.\+cc\char`\"{}$>$the code$<$/A$>$ does not require any other changes. $<$HR$>$ $<$HR$>$ \textbackslash{}section reslt Some results The figure below shows a snapshot of the $<$A \mbox{\hyperlink{two__d__unsteady__heat__2adapt_8txt_a33fad790560ed582b3fb898d4ec1067d}{H\+R\+EF}}=\char`\"{}../figures/step\+\_\+soln.\+avi\char`\"{}$>$ animated solution$<$/A$>$, obtained from the doubly adaptive simulation. @I w 0.\+75\textbackslash{}textwidth step\+\_\+soln \char`\"{}Snapshot of the solution. \char`\"{} When viewing the $<$A \mbox{\hyperlink{two__d__unsteady__heat__2adapt_8txt_a33fad790560ed582b3fb898d4ec1067d}{H\+R\+EF}}=\char`\"{}../figures/step\+\_\+soln.\+avi\char`\"{}$>$ animation of the solution$<$/A$>$, note how the \mbox{\hyperlink{two__d__unsteady__heat__2adapt_8txt_aa22034e038f07c7e249ad69406112ea2}{time}}-\/bar grows much more rapidly during phases when the solution only changes slowly, reflecting the larger timestep used during these phases. The \mbox{\hyperlink{two__d__unsteady__heat__2adapt_8txt_aa22034e038f07c7e249ad69406112ea2}{time}}-\/traces shown below compare the exact and computed solutions, and document the variations in timestep and the norm of the error throughout the simulation, for a temporal error target of \textbackslash{}c epsilon\+\_\+t = \textbackslash{}f\$ 10$^\wedge$\{-\/2\}. \textbackslash{}f\$ The plots show clearly how the adaptive timestepper selects a much larger timestep during the phases when the solution only changes slowly. However, the error during phases of rapid change is still relatively large -\/-\/ the comparison between the exact and computed solution shows that the two are not graphically indistinguishable. We ought to do better! @I w 0.\+75\textbackslash{}textwidth trace \char`\"{}Time trace of the solution, the error and the timestep chosen by the adaptive timestepper for a temporal error target of 1E-\/2. \char`\"{} The \mbox{\hyperlink{two__d__unsteady__heat__2adapt_8txt_aa22034e038f07c7e249ad69406112ea2}{time}}-\/traces below show the results from a second simulation with a smaller target error of \textbackslash{}c epsilon\+\_\+t = \textbackslash{}f\$ 10$^\wedge$\{-\/3\} \textbackslash{}f\$. The exact and computed solutions are now graphically indistinguishable and the error has been reduced significantly -\/-\/ at the cost of having to take much smaller timesteps throughout the simulation. Without adaptive \mbox{\hyperlink{two__d__unsteady__heat__2adapt_8txt_aa22034e038f07c7e249ad69406112ea2}{time}}-\/stepping, this simulation would become \textbackslash{}e very expensive as timesteps as small as \textbackslash{}f\$ dt = 2 \textbackslash{}times 10$^\wedge$\{-\/4\}\textbackslash{}f\$ are required to properly resolve the solution during the phases of rapid change. @I w 0.\+75\textbackslash{}textwidth trace\+\_\+target1e-\/3 \char`\"{}Time trace of the solution, the error and the timestep chosen by the adaptive timestepper for a temporal error target of 1E-\/3. \char`\"{} $<$HR$>$ $<$HR$>$ \textbackslash{}section comments Comments and Exercises \textbackslash{}subsection cust Customising the dump/restart procedure In two earlier examples, we commented on two undesirable features of the default dump/restart procedures\+: -\/ The restart files do not record the counter (stored in a \textbackslash{}c Doc\+Info object) that we typically use to label the output files. Therefore the output files produced in the restarted run start with label \char`\"{}0\char`\"{}, making it difficult to merge the data files from the original and restarted simulations. -\/ In an adaptive simulation, the restart files do not record the adaptive timestepper\textquotesingle{}s suggestion for the next timestep, therefore the first timestep in the restarted simulation is performed with the timestep that was used when the solution was dumped to disk, leading to slight differences in the history of the timesteps chosen}
